Respectfully.. I disagree... and yes we have had interesting discussions in the past. I remember.

When CIG mooted the idea of the $5 charge for a $0 CCU the 'outcry' was that you would be paying more than the CCU value for a chain of CCU's to any ship. The ultimate price you would have paid would be more than the in-store CCU value of the ship, you were to pay $5 for $0 added ship value. The compromise was the best one, to fold the $5 charge into the store prices of the ships so that you keep the full store CCU value you paid. CIG can charge whatever they like for their digital assets, it isn't 'stealth' anything, you can buy them at current store price or don't buy them, it's more intelligent pricing to avoid an issue in the future. You'll notice there are still ships that have the same price you can't get CCU's between them, this upsets more people than the price changes which a lot of us benefit from - which everyone knew was coming anyway, it's what fuels the 'ship shuffle game'.

Yes, those of us who got the early CCU's prior to the major ship price changes do benefit greatly over those who were either unaware or weren't around as I mentioned in my first post, but the current CCU / Warbond discounts don't even approach the same level of 'discount' and ease of application. When you add those legacy CCU's to the substantial buyback discounts, as I said I can buy back with 3 clicks of the mouse a BMM for $250 and a Carrack for $350 - multiple times, anyone trying to chain a series of Warbond CCU's together to get into the $650 - $700 ship price range are going to have to take some time and effort as well as cash outlay.. I could (and did) stock up the buyback list with buy-to-melt tokens that cost me absolutely nothing, not even waiting time, I can do it in 3 clicks at any time I don't need to wait for a Warbond CCU to fit into a chain. I don't need to wait for that rare item ship to go on sale to start a CCU chain. If you have the accrued resources - such as large amounts of store credit or cash on hand, the buy-to-melt lay-away is the easiest method to profit in the future, it's a guaranteed no loss system, ships never go down in price and you paid nothing for the stock (compared to cash tied up on account 'held' CCU's) you'll always have access to, absolutely no artificial scarcity... that's why they implemented the 'Warbond' system to reduce the use of store credit in the buy-to-melt mechanic, but it doesn't work for, or restrict those who already had their buyback lists filled up.

If you try to recoup your store credit for recycling by melting CCU's you risk the ship price changes making them either invalid or offering no / reduced discount, this doesn't happen with buyback list items, they will always have their discount, they will always be available.

Being as careful as I can I will stick to the example of what anyone can still do today, as opposed to what they could do in the past when there were far less restrictions, let me describe:

You have a ship in your hangar you paid $500 cash for it, ie it has a melt value of $500 store credit. There is a sale of a concept ship for $100 to last 10 days, you know that in a couple of years it's price is going to double, or more. So the $25 Warbond discount for cash may be enticing but it doesn't change the advantage of buyback list stockpiling with recycled credit. Just before the Concept ship sale starts you melt your $500 ship, don't worry you can buy it back at any time with store credit you already have if you have a buyback token - you only need one.

Day 1 - buy 5x $100 Concept ships with your store credit from the RSI store. No extra cash needed, CIG get no more funding from this activity.

Day 2 - melt 5x concept ships and use the store credit to buy 5x more $100 concept ships in the store. Buyback list now has 5x 'free' $100 concept ship entries that cost you nothing but a few mouse clicks.

Day 3 - melt 5x ships, buy 5x ships = 10x free $100 Concept ship tokens in your buyback list.

Day 4 - 10. Rinse and repeat recycling that $500 store credit and each day your buyback list gets 5x more buyback tokens so that by the end of the sale you have 50x buyback tokens, for absolutely no cash outlay at all. Day 11 you use the $500 store credit to buy back the first ship you melted, ergo your 'game' and account hangar are exactly the same as the moment before the Concept Ship sale started. You can still buy the $75 Warbond discounted Concept Ship, nothing described above stops you.

CIG increases the price of that concept ship - now for every buyback list entry you can get that ship at the original $100 price , at any time, each $100 gives you a new ship of value $200, and you have 50 of them that cost you nothing, absolutely nothing... and that's just one ship. This is why LTI was removed from credit sold concept ships because they know people were buy-to-melt stockpiling LTI tokens. On the day they instituted the buyback list was talking to another Concierge member on another platform about what it all meant, and I can't remember whether it was him or me that first used the term 'LTI token', many people are confused by this term, it is not a ship that has LTI, that is just a ship. A 'token' in this sense is a promise from CIG that you can always get an item you don't currently own for a discounted / fixed price - that is the entry in your buyback list, they are the 'tokens' whether they have LTI or not, they are the guarantee that you'll always be able to get that item even if it is restricted for sale in the store, you can have a CCU 'token' in your buyback list to guarantee future access to a restricted sale ship.

The buy-to-melt mechanic, that still exists today if in somewhat more limited form than it was, still affords those same potentially huge discounts in the future depending on what the prices of ships become - this is why you can't get CCU's to the very large ships they feel would unbalance the game if they were available in large numbers. If you had no buyback list discount tokens you would have to use the current RSI store to buy any base ship to apply your stockpiled CCU's to, the higher the base price ship the less 'discount' you are likely to get, the lower the base price the more likely there is to be a wait to complete the CCU chain or any melted CCU's have now become useless to buy back, whereas if I have a stock of say 50x $30 ships with LTI which I can get at any time I have much more scope to use any stockpiled CCU's chained for maximum discount...

...as long as that buyback list allows what it does the problem will always remain even if they abolished CCU's altogether. My buyback list is the most useful because it gives me the biggest discounts coupled with the freedom to use it at any time I choose, no artificial scarcity for me. As I said just like you I haven't paid anywhere near full price for any new concept because of the buyback list, I don't have to wait for sales of ships that fit into any CCU chain I might have, and yes I do have them. If I did sell ships off-site I could have a store front populated with my buyback list options, and the eager 'enthusiasts' think I'm just a nice helpful guy letting them have one of my ships at no extra cost (with LTI they can't get in the RSI store) but really I'm taking their cash money, using my buyback list discount and keeping the extra there is no limit on me buying from my buyback list for cash.. which of course makes it a lot easier the next time a concept ship sale happens, I don't need to dig into my own pockets. Add to that, I'm getting plenty kudos and Concierge status goodies because I'm using cash to buy multiples of ships even though they are discounted, which add up on my account. The obvious marker being that although I've spent thousands on my account as far as CIG are concerned I've given away thousands of dollars worth of ships to 'friends'.. their received 'gifts' don't add to their Concierge status, but their cash to me does boost my Concierge status.

So tell me how laboriously stockpiling CCU's, which if I want a substantial discount for I've got to spend cash, in a mad race during any sale period (which I would potentially lose the benefit of if I melt them later) is easier than the buyback list 'buy-to-melt' zero-cost-to-me guaranteed future availability and future profit?

As I said, CIG customer services were distracted by the stockpiling of CCU's annoyance in 2016 / 2017, when they should have thought more about the buyback list potential abuse. The credit token was a waste of time once the buyback lists were already populated, it only affects people who don't misuse the system now. The Warbond sales (the restriction on credit use rather than discounts) only partially addresses the issue but the one measure which would guarantee there was no profit to abusing the 'generosity' (insert eye-roll here) of the marketing division would be to end the ability to always buy back ships at the original price paid... just like they did with CCU's. They could also say that you can't melt any standalone ship for a minimum of 14 days which would prevent buy-to-melt recycling. There is no other company that would offer the same facility to their customers to be able to endlessly exchange and re-buy goods at the original price forever. There are those who think I'm an inveterate white knight, but as you can see, I'm under no delusions that CIG might be lacking in their ability to look at their systems and realise they might be stockpiling future problems. @Zyloh-CIG Blaming the customer is not the answer. 'If you build it they will come' is the adage, and marketing division built this edifice even in the face of many calls to think again... they were laser focused on facilitating a group in the community which Sandi now happily calls 'snowflakes' on camera.

It's odd. My April 2014 account, which is my main account - this one, got only the Monkey envelope. My 2021 second account got the Ram and the Monkey envelope, and my 3 other 2022 accounts all got the Monkey envelope.

I did say the worse culprit is the buyback at original price. I don't see the relevance of discussing the $5 CCU charge, the fact that they removed the $0 CCU option is enough to paint the accurate picture.

We have been suggesting this to them from the very beginning, only allow purchase of CCU's for ships you already have on your account and apply them automatically at checkout, unfortunately the noisy few who were making the most use of the CCU exploit were more 'noisy'.

Every measure they instituted only disadvantaged bona-fide players, it hardly affected the offsite selling at all, Warbond CCU's replaced $0 CCU's as the 'go-to' exploit to make money when Warbond was supposed to stop it. We've pointed this out to them many many times.

They did start to remove $0 CCU's from accounts back in 2017 but they made a mistake, some CCU's became $0 (or negative dollar) after ship price changes that had not existed before so that CCU's that some backers paid money for were removed - so they halted the process of deleting them from accounts after only a few days, and they never started it again. It never occurred to them to start with those accounts that had the most 'gifting' going on in them. We pointed out the exploit potential to them from the day they put the facilities in to allow it to happen, when they didn't respond we thought the best thing to do was make everyone aware of those exploits so that it wasn't just a greedy few who would benefit from the weakness of the system. We never expected them to allow it to continue for years.

You don't need $0 CCU's to make money from selling ships, the buyback list stockpiled with credit bought 'buy to melt' ships can do that just fine, massively inflated buyback lists are the problem more than CCU's. There is no limit on the number of ships you can get from your buyback list with cash... and if someone else is giving you cash then you don't need 'credit tokens', they were a merely an inconvenience to 'real' backers, they were never (and still aren't) a problem for the profiteers.

It wasn't the $0 CCU's that allowed the most egregious exploits, they were just the biggest annoyance to customer services and that was a deliberate strategy to deflect attention away from the buy back list exploit, it was the buyback list that allowed someone to buy back any melted ship or game package at the original price they paid (on my account I can buy back several ships and game packages at original concept price with LTI, a BMM for $250 with LTI for example). If you knew there was a 10 day sale and you had $250 cash during the concept sale you buy the BMM on day one, day 2 melt the BMM and rebuy with store credit, rinse and repeat for the next 9 days, every melt puts one copy into your buyback list forever so that even though you only spent $250 cash on day one of the sale, you ended up with 10x $250 LTI BMM's in your buy back list, you can go back to your buyback list and buy that BMM for $250 today even though it now costs $650 in the store without LTI. Every buy back list BMM concept sale token you collected back in 2016 for no more cost than 3 mouse clicks 'saves you' $400 compared to today's store prices, and there are dozens of other ships with similar store price increases since they were concepted. The Carrack for example, and the Orion.

If they changed the system so that buybacks had to be at todays store prices just like CCU's the off-site sellers would virtually disappear overnight because they don't keep stocks of ships they paid actual money for on their accounts, there is no restriction to gifting if the base ship was bought with cash and why would having cash be a problem if someone else is giving you the cash in the first place? Without direct player to player gifting of ships there would never have been a problem. They don't need to pay to keep stock on their accounts as long as they have access to a stocked up buyback list which guarantees a permanent ever-increasing discount for them. I've got plenty on my account I haven't paid full store price for any ship that has had a CCU to it since 2016, every time they increase the price of a ship they make my next 'big-job ship' store purchase cheaper because they made it possible and they kept it possible even after being advised about that exploitation potential. It's not a bug, it's the feature they intended.

Up to now the ticket price has been around $100.

They will choose a venue that can accommodate at least 1000 people, probably closer to 2000 or more.

There is usually a very long queue to get in and they invariably open the doors late, at Manchester it took over 2 hours to get everyone in through security checks. When it rained in Manchester while we waited outside they came and gave us free umbrellas. If you have a bag they will search it but they generally don't do body searches aside from metal detectors.

There will be a place with multiple vendors for food and drinks - expensive, overpriced. At the 2015 CitizenCon in Manchester the food was provided but you had to pay for drinks at the bar. It was a more 'barcitizen' type feel in 2015 I had a long chat with Erin Roberts there, whereas the 2019 Manchester CitCon had a much more 'corporate managed' feel. It's unlikely they will choose a venue that has included catering now.

There will be some sort of display, at the last in Manchester it was the entrance foyer Carrack ice carving being made. At previous CitCon's they have had large ship models. there will be a lot of 'event type' banners and imagery relating to 'in-lore fiction'.

There will be a cosplay competition and some community members will be roaming around in their cosplay gear.

You get a 'swag bag' with stuff in it, but often they aren't organised enough to give them out at the door and you may have to go back and get them. You'll have a security tag and wristband.

During the event, for meal breaks etc, there will be dev team members you can talk to and the senior members usually have a table for signing stuff like posters and Chairmans Club Handbooks / taking selfies. Long queue, time limited, this is not the time to chat to the team members.

There will be booths for organisations to recruit from or for Streamers / Youtubers you can meet and greet, they give out merch.
There will be booths for 'official approved' merchandise sellers.

At the last CitCon one of the booths was 3 developers designing the Sextant which was part of the digital CitizenCon client reward.

Here are some videos I took at the last Manchester CitizenCon - just skip your way through them. I recommend you bring a camera and tripod as well as your phone if you can.

Many people have given the correct answer, that it is one game universe with a single-player campaign set in it, but by also stating that the definitive answer is 'unknown now'.. that's the part that isn't true. We have been told that Squadron 42 takes place inside the Star Citizen universe exactly as it was originally described. Jared Huckaby, a couple of years ago, described Squadron 42 as 'One huge dynamic mission inside the PU'. This has never changed.

Anyone who thinks that Squadron 42 is unnecessary, or not relevant to their Star Citizen experience, simply doesn't understand what the project is about. It's hard for some to wrap their head around I know but the current PU is a playable alpha small-scale limited demo. There's a reason the coming star systems all link into the star systems in Squadron 42 (check it on the Star Map), because you'll be going through those star systems to get to start Squadron 42. You have to 'sign up' from within the PU.

The important part to remember is that in both games you can play the exact same character if you chose to, you retire from military service into a free-roam persistent universe where Squadron 42 is recent history and the parts of the universe, the characters and the organisations in Squadron 42, can and will remain in the PU, some of them will know you from your time in Squadron 42.

While in the military you have a military history log and you can collect and own items and money (you get military pay), those go with you when you retire to 'the verse'. NPC AI in Star Citizen will refer to your exploits in Squadron 42, some will consider you a hero, others may consider you the jackboot heel of the hated militaristic UEE. Some side missions will start in Squadron 42 and continue in the PU. You will be faced with choices in Squadron 42, the choices you make will directly affect how you are treated in the PU and may even lead to content, like places you can go or 'people you can interact with' in the PU only ex-military (those who played Squadron 42) can access, like the Helios system or the Kilian system for example. Chris talked about this in 2018 during the CitizenCon presentation when he mentioned USO-type clubs for ex-military, he also talked about it in 2016 during a Squadron 42 special Q&A, you can see references to it in the lore.

The Vanduul war does not end with Squadron 42 Episode One, it will be still going on when the PU launches yet you'll notice the current PU doesn't reference the Vanduul War anywhere (it is referenced in advertising blurb and videos relating to military service - Invictus Launch Week for example) because from your current player perspective in the PU it hasn't happened yet. Go and read the Hurston Dynamics Corp history wall, a major arms manufacturer for the UEE and it's role in the Vanduul War isn't mention in that history timeline.

The difficulty some have is that they miss the fact that the clock starts ticking as soon as you enter the games' universe (this what they refer to as 'persistent'), either the PU or Squadron 42, you can't go back in time with the same character and the game world is not separated like other games with a multiplayer tacked on - the PU timeline always moves forward and so does the timeline in Squadron 42. You play the game in real time and the only thing you can do is pause time or move forward time via sleeping, very similar to Skyrim V except you don't choose your save game, the game does and it's always the last saved game spot you move on from.

This is why it has to be a single-player campaign because the choices your character makes have to be yours alone. The only way to play the game making different choices in Squadron 42 is to start the whole campaign again with a brand new character, which is why in the Death of a Spaceman letter to the community they talked about 'character slots'. This is why some older backers in the community know to have multiple game packages because they ARE character slots - even though they are a tiny minority. Those who wonder about future funding don't realise, some Squadron 42 character slots will be repeat sales to existing customers.

You can replay the combat sections of Squadron 42 in the Arena Commander simulator, cooperatively with friends, but of course because it is not in the game universe it doesn't affect your characters' history. This was exactly the same in Wing Commander Prophecy, you couldn't go back in time with a character and you could only replay the combat sections in the 'in-verse' simulator.

Just like the real world there is training and experiences you gain in the military - example a lot of civilian airline pilots trained in the military - it will be the same in the PU, you will need 'licenses' for vehicles and certain equipment that is limited use. If you join the PU as a civilian you'll have to have a pilots license to be able to fly a ship. Certain mission types will require you to have security clearances you can only get in the military. There will be certain places in the PU where only military and ex-military are allowed to go. Frontline military equipment and ships (the F8C Lightning for example) are only legally owned and used by those who gained the license to own and use them from the military or by special award for service via the UEE government (Chairmans Club), civilians without military experience won't legally be allowed to own and operate the F8C, which means you can't go to a ship store and buy it. This is why in the current PU they keep referring to the 'relevant combat experience' in missions like Xenothreat or Siege of Orison. The idea is that as ex-military you are expected to 'keep current' with frontline military equipment, but civilians aren't allowed to own and operate ships (legally) if they are a significant threat to UEE forces.

Have you ever been to Klescher Rehabilitation Facility? Have you noticed that when you have served your time and can leave the announcer voice refers to you as 'civilian'?

Citizenship can be achieved 3 ways:
You can buy it - it will be expensive.
You can earn it via assisting UEE forces, like the Advocacy via the CDF for example - it will take a long time.
You get it awarded immediately you sign up for military service - the only way for a player to do that currently is by starting Squadron 42.

You cannot earn or buy ex-military status without starting Squadron 42.

Citizenship can be revoked by the UEE - for criminal activity and criminal history for example.

Whether you are a citizen or a civilian, whether you are ex-military or not, will have a very big impact on your experience within the Star Citizen universe because it's all connected, it is all one big universe. The current Alpha PU doesn't represent the final intended game experience, not even close.

For the first time ever (afaik) outside of their Youtube / Twitch channels they have spent money on advertising the game (including Squadron 42) on Reddit in the last month.

I see these posts about being griefed and ganked and I wonder if they are playing the same game I am or even the same game that most Youtubers and Twitch streamers I watch are playing.

I play for hours and never get any issue except bugs, mainly in PTU. I played Siege of Orison and found that the other players were more than happy to cooperate, several healed me without even asking - most just ignored me. All you have to do is accept the mission and hang back to automagically earn 400K+ / hour. I've been looting bodies for armour and weapons while the mission was ongoing! I've spent many hours looting bodies on Solanki platform without any ongoing mission alongside other players doing the same thing and no-one bothers anyone. If you get to the good stuff first it's yours, if they get there first it's theirs. There's more than enough gear to go around. Someone claiming the FS9 is the OP weapon in the game, you can pick up around 3 - 5 of them, plus ammo, for every visit to Solanki platform and you can do several visits per hour. Go naked, gear up, go back store the gear in local inventory, come back naked and repeat until you get thoroughly bored and your inventory has enough to last you as long as you need so that if you lose an outfit/weapons you have them replaced before you've even left the hospital room.

Last night I was around Port Olisar and on Cellin (PTU) going around the outposts just looting, saw a couple of other players, they never bothered me.

Generally I just leave if there are other ships around POI's, it's no problem to go elsewhere and come back later. Also.. don't park your ship and leave it full of stuff you wouldn't want to lose, no-one else can access local inventories that are holding your stuff. Don't keep all your eggs in one basket unless you have to and if you do, get in and get out as fast as possible. Never request hangar doors to be opened unless your shields are fully charged and you're ready to zoom out as soon as the doors open.

There are fairly easy skills to adapt to that reduce your chances of being caught unaware. When you come out of QT get up to max speed asap, don't dawdle, get your drive spooled up and a QT POI chosen asap, any.. it doesn't matter as long as it's away from where the trouble is. If there is someone there choose an empty area of space to zoom into then decouple and turn to face them, they are coming onto your guns and missiles while you are flying away from theirs, their closing time to your weapons is reduced while the closing time between their weapons and missiles to you is extended... in this situation they can't even use noise and flares because they get ejected behind them but you can, if they turn to avoid your fire they can't catch you fast enough to stop you jumping out. You can fire missiles while the QT drive is calibrating so choose your QT POI appropriately. If you mostly do the single-player shoot and scoot defensive play you don't need gimbals. If they are using QT snares, which is very rare, then get out of the POI to POI traffic lanes, easy enough.

The reason so many 'die' is because they are so much in a rush to do what they want to do they don't plan or take a little more time to prepare. Just last night someone was complaining the only rock worth mining was Quantanium, that shows the attitude, it has to be get rich quick with minimal thought time and effort or the game is just 'bad' in their view. You don't need millions of credits to play the game and there's hardly any point in buying ships in the game - soon to be wiped - when you can rent them. It costs 51.5K to rent a Prospector for a day, you can make enough to rent 2 in just over an hour easily, no more worries about wait timers.. you'll be back on the job within 10 minutes of being 'ganked' if you thought ahead.

I have the 'big job' multi-crew ships, but there's not much point in taking them out and then complaining about the reclaim timer if you aren't going to 'multi-crew' the multi-crew ships. You can rent plenty of ships with reclaim timers of less than 2 minutes to do most of what you want, and it is fairly easy to make enough credits to keep spares of components and stuff in your local spawn point inventory. Vary it up a bit, combine activities to maximise income. Some looting / selling, some box delivery missions, some light trading, some wreck / cave raiding - you can do these things all at once. I scratch my head and wonder why so many think they can only do 'one mission at a time'. The game is supposed to simulate living a future life, no-one lives a life where they only ever do one activity to the exclusion of all others.

Just going around looting boxes at outposts can bring in over 100K / hour if you take the time to learn where to look, I never have to buy weapons or armour (and that's without doing any missions) and I have loads of them by the end of the first day on a patch, because they are 'free' I can go anywhere and not worry about losing them because they'll be replaced faster than I can lose them. You only have to do one bunker mission to get enough weapons and armour to last a month - if you plan ahead and accept there is a little grind involved... this gets waaay easier if you buddy up with just one other person.

Painting the game as some endless grief-fest is just so wide-of-the-mark-untrue it can't be anything else other than trolling to scare of the curious from what I see, 99% of the time I play by myself and hardly ever get any bother. There was a Youtuber brand new to the game a few days ago, relied totally on chat to show him the ropes and he played solidly - live - for 4 hours+... got fully stocked up with gear, with credits to spare, and he wasn't even getting the most helpful advice. What do people expect to achieve in 4 hours total play time? There is nothing wrong with the game, it is not 'unbalanced', most get by just fine, however some lack the problem solving skills and patience for a game of this type... Don't worry Arena Commander is there for the needs of those types of players.

It is not clear what you're asking exactly, so rather let's talk about how servers are loaded currently and how they will be loaded when server meshing comes online.

All the information about the game space has to written to the server hard drive. There is one game build which contains all of the Stanton system objects and it is loaded to every server hard drive whether anyone is using parts of that space or not. All this duplicated data transfer has to carried over the network that controls the servers. Server Object Container Streaming determines if an area in the Stanton system is being used or not and so if it isn't it is streamed out of server RAM and back in as needed, the information about the game build remains on the server hard drive as long as it is running. There was local (running) persistence but once a server is shut down there is no persistence, the server is wiped and all player activity not recorded to the player database (anything in storage for example) is lost. Each server is loaded with an exact same copy of the game world as the dev's built it with player owned assets loaded in afterward.

The server game build is going to change to allow smaller parts of the game universe to be loaded onto server hard drives, one planet and it's moons per server for example, the servers are then meshed to allow seamless transition between different servers' area of authority. This is static server meshing and 'sharding'. The Stanton system can be broken over several servers hard drives with each server having a fixed (static) boundary of authority. Server Object Container Streaming still controls what is loaded into RAM, according to player activity.

Dynamic Server Meshing refers to the ability of the server to expand or contract it's boundary of authority within a shard, this means dynamically writing / re-writing to the hard drive of a server as it is running to expand or contract it's area of authority within a shard. It is more efficient because each server can expand and contract it's area of authority according to what players are doing. It could contain the whole game universe or, multiple star systems, or just one building. It is also efficient because it avoids huge (potentially unused) data writes to every server hard drive.

Persistent Entity Streaming does a very similar thing to Object Container Streaming except that the information is not stored on the servers local hard drive to load into RAM, it is kept on a remote network and called as players demand - so that if you (or any player) are in an area PES will say if there are things there - which are not part of the games base build features - which should be added and what state they should be in when they are added. Entity Graph keeps a record of all dynamic objects in the game and sends a 'snapshot record' back to the persistence database every few seconds to milliseconds so that database can inform any servers spinning up about the total state of the game universe... including any mines your Nautilus has laid.

Does that make things clearer for you?

What is the drive on the new 'old' PC formatted to? Are you sure it is NTFS?

Have you installed the RSI Launcher to the default address and the game to the default address?

It is best not to install Star Citizen and the RSI Launcher within the protected Windows file system structure (like the folder 'Program Files' for example) because you can run in to folder access permissions with Windows. It often fails as you describe when the Launcher and Star Citizen game folder are installed to different drives.

1. Make sure the drive you want to install the game to is formatted to NTFS.

2. Create a folder in the root of that drive ie D:/RSI/ - this is now your game root folder. If you don't have a separate drive then install the RSI Launcher to a folder on the root of your C drive. ie C:/RSI/

3. Uninstall the RSI Launcher completely, re-install to the game root folder you created. ie D:/RSI/ or C:/RSI/

4. In the game root folder you should see a folder called RSI Launcher. Copy the StarCitizen folder and contents to this same folder, your game root folder called 'RSI'. If you have been changing install directories it may have messed up the StarCitizen folder structure, make sure there isn't a folder inside the StarCitizen folder called 'StarCitizen'. If there is just re-copy the folder from your laptop to the game root folder ('RSI') and delete all the folders in the 'Program Files/Roberts Space Industries' directory.

5. Run the RSI Launcher, sign in - DO NOT HIT INSTALL. Top right go to 'Settings' tab and scroll down to where it says 'Library Folder' make sure the game root folder address is there ie 'D:/RSI/'

6. Hit 'Verify', the manifest will download and then any files needed to update.

Good luck.

CPU (central processing unit) is a generalized processor that is designed to carry out a wide variety of tasks (in sequential fashion), for example positioning vertices in a given volume of space on a 3D model or creating a Word document. GPU (graphics processing unit) is a specialized processing unit with enhanced mathematical computation capability, ideal for computer graphics and machine-learning tasks, it's role is specific, to put an image on a screen. The enhanced computational ability of a GPU can also be used to do high speed hash rates for such things as Bitcoin mining, it's made into a 'one trick pony'. To put it in the simplest terms a GPU is designed to be a fast number cruncher repeating the same task very fast whereas a CPU is more of a data organiser using many algorithms.

1. There is a difference between cold and frigid. There is plant life on Earth that can survive sub-zero temperatures even flowering plants - like Edelweiss for instance, it's likely the plant life on microTech has been adapted to do so even more.

You don't need constant minus 40 degrees to cool electronic hardware and it is also well to remember that soil surface temperatures receiving direct sunlight are not the same as deep soil temperatures without sunlight. I see no immersion breaking, it's perfectly possible that under-surface temperatures are sufficient for hardware cooling needs. In an internal environment fit for human habitation cooling below the dew point would be hazardous to electronics because of condensation... if you're going to extrapolate from current technology and Earth-based viewpoints.

2. They are well aware of the immersion breaking appearance of the hover mechanic for thrusters, where the issue lies is that those thrusters have to operate in space and on planetary surfaces. Real world physics is applied to thruster output it just looks unrealistic because of the limitations of inertia. If those thrusters were only capable of producing a few G's of thrust to make them seem believable planetside then coming to a halt in space after reaching speeds of thousands of metres per second would take many minutes, not seconds, to achieve. The thrusters are grossly overpowered for planetside use because they are tuned to give reasonable stopping distances in space. You can't have both (right now), you can't stop a ship in seconds with the same thrusters you expect to struggle to hold a ship up against 1G or less.

Master modes may seem immersion breaking until you take into account this problem of inertia at very high velocities - 1000 m/s is 2237 mph slowing from 1000m/s to zero in 15 seconds means you would be experiencing deceleration at a rate of 67 m/s equivalent to going from 150 mph to zero in 1 second, for 15 seconds. The more mass a ship has the more inertia it has relative to it's velocity. You wouldn't want realistic stopping times in this game, it's also unlikely you would want an Expanse style mechanic of needing to turn your ships ass toward whatever your destination was for a significant portion of it's travel to said destination.

There are those who say that having max velocities in space travel is immersion breaking, but is it? Modern aircraft have overspeed protection systems. The IFCS in Star Citizen performs the same function, you can never fully disable it while your ship is powered on because a part of it's design is not to exceed human body tolerances. If you could reach velocities of 100's of thousands of km/h it would take hours to slow down at survivable deceleration speeds and even a few degrees course correction at that speed would squash you flatter than a pancake against the ships hull, your neck would snap and your restraint harness would cut you in half first of course.

Even if they do go for absolute realism that doesn't solve the problem of the human body which couldn't survive deceleration from 1000+ m/s to 0 m/s in mere seconds even if the ship hull structure could. Star Trek handwavium for this problem of inertia at high velocities is solved by 'Inertial Dampeners', Master Mode is the handwavium required for Star Citizen to be tolerable and survivable at above space combat maneuvering cruise speeds. There's a good reason Kerbal Space Program is so hard for players to get into, and probably why they don't have human pilots.

4. Understanding the above explanation of inertia and thrust to weight ratio would make this point moot, of course ships with more mass are going to struggle in a gravity well compared to lower mass ships, and when cargo has mass this will be even more evident, there is such a thing as maximum thruster technology capability. It's just like jet engines today, there comes a point where jet engines just don't function, or are not feasible to manufacture, above a certain size. There is an efficiency cost benefit analysis to be made, for every extra thruster you need more power and more fuel so that in effect your ships is basically tending toward mostly thruster mass dotted all over the hull, battery / capacitors and fuel tank increase the mass further and because of all that extra mass you need more thrusters and so a limit is reached.

That's the point isn't it? Starfield is going to be good, of that I have no doubt, and it is nice to see a company of Bethesda's size move to the space game genre but make no bones about it even with all their resources and a fairly comparable development time frame you won't be able to do in Starfield what you can do in Star Citizen right now. Elite Dangerous is a good example, they have been in continual development for a similar length of time but they opted for a truncated 'get the product out' experience releasing a feature limited game in the expectation that it will expand and improve, but the law of diminishing returns applies, with each release that falls short they get fewer new players and more existing players leave choosing not to buy the addons.

I think this phenomenon factored into the decision making with No Mans Sky, if they hadn't released updates and addons free of charge to existing game owners we would likely have seen the same, a diminishing player base showcasing the game less and less to new prospects.

Part of the reason SC is popular among Youtubers and streamers, even the negative ones, is that there is always something to discuss, always something new to show off.. in a word.. for the streamer that means content that is always new and fresh. There is always the dream of things to come, anyone who discounts that is not being realistic about this project. The day SC is announced as finished that feature of the project begins to die and the sum toto of what is achieved has to stand on it's own merits in a competitive game industry that is not above copying the successes of other games. Bethesda will be banking on the notion that their game, without the hard stuff, will be enough for their fans and they are probably right. No-one in their right mind seriously suggests that because you play one game you can't play another especially if the buy-in price is no deterrent to having both. I actually think that Starfield will draw more new players to Star Citizen looking for a more expansive experience, just like Elite Dangerous and No Mans Sky has.

Few take into account back in 2012 space games without swords, magic and dragons were considered a poor investment by the 'suits' that decide what game you are going to play in the next cycle. If it hadn't been for the revival of franchises like Star Trek and Star Wars or the popularity of TV series like The Expanse, space games would likely still be a niche gaming experience. Even the advent of the billionaire race to space has likely had some impact on what futuristic visions of the gaming industry corporate developers have, once they find a formula that works they stick to it no matter how many versions of Mass Effect there are you won't be landing the Normandy on a free roam planet, you won't be taking it's shuttle planetside without a cutscene. Why bother? The fans don't expect it anyway and they'll still pay for more of the same. GTA despite all it's iterations and billions of dollars in revenue is still basically the same game it was at first release. Is there anyone daring to suggest that GTA 6 will / should feature an international crime syndicate multi-city game experience? Why not? Do you think the fans of the game wouldn't go crazy for that?

Star Citizen solely relies on players showcasing existing features and discussing upcoming features. Procedural generation refers to any method of asset creation that doesn't involve hand sculpting, which is long and dev time expensive. Using greyscale images to offset faces from a flat 3D mesh has been in use for many years. First you choose the mesh grid according to the detail level you require, this basically is selecting the number of rows and columns, it's called subdividing.

Next you take a greyscale image and using the 0 - 255 pixel values from black to white apply that as the multiplier to the height above the base mesh - this is why they are commonly referred to as height maps. You can get greyscale imagery from radar terrain mapping if you want to take from real world terrain examples. This is called a 'displacement modifier'.

The limitation of height map displacement was that the height values are calculated on the GPU for the visual representation but the collision physics etc were calculated on the original non-transformed mesh. This is why you can see someone walking on terrain and they sink into the ground.

To retain the heightmap information for a 3D model you would need to 'bake' the heightmap displacement data into a transformed 3Dmesh, this produces a higher detail mesh according to the number of times you subdivide the mesh and the number of pixels on your terrain bitmap, once you bake in the calculated values a new 3D mesh is created and the flat mesh is discarded, now your terrain mesh has collision physics and topography.

Evo Herzeg did work on this problem and has managed to create a system that works in engine where the GPU heightmap calculations are passed back to the CPU for collision physics to take place.

For years heightmaps were used to make simple 3D models appear more complex by the same method, commonly referred to as nurnies or greebles, this method was developed because game engines had polygon limits which made the game models look simplistic or brought frame rates to a crawl if they were overly detailed. Other advancements also allowed RGB bitmaps to inform lighting of the model. This became known as PBR - Physically Based Rendering (this is a very simplified explanation of PBR but it covers the basics for our purposes here).

EDIT as an aside CI are further advancing heightmaps from simple grey scale to allow something that GS heightmaps don't - displacement in 3 dimensions rather than just height. You can't get overhangs with simple GS heightmaps, but they will be able to do it with RGB heightmaps.

The game developers at Cloud Imperium use both methods, they use heightmaps (with extended functionality) to create 3D models of planets from smooth spheres without the need for 3D modellers to hand craft a whole area. These are baked into the final models which are not full detail as yet, that final stage of added detail is done in the game engine using PBR.

There are many 3D modeller programs you can use this heightmap technique on - the 2 that I have used are blender and DAZ3D, although DAZ3D doesn't allow the 'baking in' it does allow the visual representation of heightmaps.

Unreal Engine can import Photogrammetry once it has been converted to an FBX file, you can do this online it renders the pixels of the textures applied to the base model rather than the base mesh (again very simplified), you could see this as an evolution of PBR - they call this Nanite.

Photogrammetry does not use heightmaps, it uses AI to calculate the relative dimensions of an object photographed from multiple angles based upon pixel shading. Of course you an use all 3 methods in UE, but to make a 3D model you'll need an external app for that.

Hope that helps.

They won't, the spaces are designed so that viewing from one space into another space is kept to a minimum. The players looking out of the spaceport window can't see the interior of a Javelin. The people on the Javelin can't see the interior of the spaceport. It's a hard notion to wrap your head around that the exterior of a ship can be on one DGS and the interior of that same ship can be on another DGS, but that is how it's done.

At the extreme they can be on their own server and they will be persisted from the time they exit QT to the time they enter QT. You have to get in an elevator from the docking port up to the space station interior so the space station is one server while the ship (and the docking arm and lobby) is on another server, or the DGS to DGS transfer can take place in the airlock

Yes, that limit exists, but it's not in the 1000 range, it's higher than that.. and even piled close together 10,000's of objects cover a wide area so occlusion culling, off-screen culling, ship interior culling and LOD's do factor in to what is feasible.

Seamless transfer of players and NPC's would be visible if not carried out in areas was where no-one can see them. Which is why they are doing away with open pads where ships de-spawn and switching to enclosed hangars. Port Olisar was designed before the requirements of server meshing transfer between DGS's and Shards was known, it has no elevators and hangars

Sharding is not ultimately due to the limits of server meshing, it is due to the real world signal travel time between regional centres. Ping time if you will. There will be regional shards for a long time to come which has nothing to do with Cloud Imperium game design.

Why do you think that? If all you are rendering is one space station and the medium distant LOD for a planet there's no reason that either your PC or the server can't handle that 1000 player load. There is such things as occlusion culling... it's very unlikely you'll have direct line of sight to every single player and every item they are wearing / holding. So yes, the game will decide who can see what and remove what isn't visible.

Yes they will be visible if they are on the same shard, and which shard you all go to is determined by match logc as much as is practicable.

The game spaces inside structures are not big enough to hold a 1000 players all in the same volume in line of sight of each other except on planet / moon surfaces or in space, and any places that perhaps could will have traffic flow management to reduce that possibility. In which case things like ship interior culling, building interior culling and LOD's comes into play to reduce workload on the client PC.

I did say Port Olisar was a bad example, it hasn't been designed for server meshing, the more up-to-date space stations have which is why they have elevators.

3. The seamless transition between DGS's and shards.

This is required because if you broke the game space into smaller and smaller areas, without meshing you would have what other games have, a cutscene transfer every time you moved from area to area.
The amount of players in a small game area is limited by the volume that area has, you just couldn't get 1000 players into a small corridor, a bar or a shop but let's say they are all mad keen to go to that place at the same time. In order to get to the place they have to pass through these traffic managed choke points and those DGS to DGS / shard to shard 'transfer possible' limited spaces like elevators.

The process works the same for both DGS to DGS transfer and shard to shard transfer, shard to shard may take a little longer.

There is 1000 players milling about in TEASA Spaceport between the train platform and the lobby area where the elevators go to the hangars - there are 8 elevators each can take 10 players to a hangar, which means the they can take away up to 80 players at a time. Players are coming in on trains and leaving via the hangars. Max capacity for that DGS on EU Shard 001 holding TEASA Spaceport has been reached. Remember that DGs isn't holding any other part of the game universe, only the area from the tunnel before TEASA Spaceport to the hangar elevators is in that servers RAM, it can sealiy hold 1000 players on foot in that area.

The system has predicted ahead of time that there are too many players coming in on trains to TEASA Spaceport on EU Shard 001, so trains entering tunnels with 50 players on each are duplicated to a newly spun up EU Shard 002 that holds the game space from the tunnel exit just before the TEASA Spaceport platform to the exit from TEASA Spaceport via the hangars, there are now two shards holding TEASA Spaceport.

All the players on a train carriage and the train carriage itself are momentarily duplicated to both Shard 001 and Shard 002, you see all the other players in the carriage on Shard 001, they are looking and behaving exactly the same on Shard 002 because all the data and control inputs sent to both shards are the same,this only happens for a few seconds at most while the train is in the tunnel.

All I have to now is kill the train carriage on Shard 001 and let the train carriage on Shard 002 (with your identical copies) continue out of the tunnel to the now much quieter TEASA Spaceport. I've also reduced the numbers of players entering TEASA Spaceport on Shard 001, because they were the evil copies of the 50 players and I killed them! There are many trains going through tunnels in Lorville, I can do this shard to shard duplicate/kill transfer as many times as I like to manage traffic flow. No player saw it happen because they could only see the players in the train carriage they were on while in that tunnel, they certainly can't see 1000 other players on that train.

You say.. but I was in one train while my buddy was on another train but we both want to go to the same ship hangar at TEASA Spaceport, he's on Shard 001 and I'm on Shard 002 now so we can't see each other or interact! What happens then is that now that Shard 001 has been de-populated somewhat, when you get into the elevator to go to the hangar, that elevator sets off on Shard 002, but it arrives back on Shard 001 to the hangar you chose by exactly the same process as you left Shard 001, you have no idea that you transferred twice between shards. When the player numbers pressure on Shard 001 reduces, Shard 002 can transfer all it's occupants back to Shard 001 and be spun done completely, it may have been up for only 20 minutes and it only ever had authority for that small section of TEASA Spaceport.

2. Managing the Game Space and traffic control measures.

The game space is broken up into areas that are very small, much smaller than people realise. Some think that the smallest area that has to go on a DGS is a planet or moon, but a planet or moon could be spread over hundreds of DGS's, and there would be no overlap of authority between those DGS's. A landing zone like Orison could be spread over 30 - 40 DGS's (or more!) each holding 500 or more players (that could be 20,000 players in one landing zone). Remember only one DGS in a shard is allowed to write it's change state information to the Entity Graph for a given area.

How do you break a landing zone into 30 or 40 areas? What you need is a time when players are in a confined area for up to a few seconds, without any external view from the small space they are in so they couldn't see 1000 other players even if they wanted to while they are in that confined space - an elevator, a store, a bar, a space station, a train carriage in a tunnel would suit our purpose.

The commonest question is 'How can they possibly put 1000's of players in an area within sight of each other, and the answer is, they won't because they don't need to. Again the common response is 'What if the players all go there how could they stop them all being in the same place at the same time!'. If you drive a car you already know the answer to that, you just haven't transferred that understanding to the game.

You have a car with 4 seats, 4 people at maximum capacity. you want to drive into town it's the busiest part of the day on the weekend lot's of other cars with 4 people in are going into town. How could you stop the town centre from becoming overloaded? You manage the traffic flow, you have traffic lights slow down groups of cars and let them through only as enough people leave the town centre so that on average the outflow matches the inflow.

In the game these checkpoints (traffic light equivalents) are orbital security, ATC, hangar access and guards, elevators, guarded access ways you have to pass through all designed to slow down progress and manage inflow / outflow to an area. The game system can predict ahead if the volume of traffic is heading in a direction and make changes - like ordering guards at access points to start scanning players more frequently. Thius is exactly the same way they do it in an airport... they manage how many planes are landing per hour and how fast people entering the airport get through the airport to the gates. Unlike the real world the game can, and will take any excess overflow and transfer them to a whole new shard, even temporarily. How can that work?

That is not how it works anyone who is on your shard close enough to be visible to you will be visible to you. You'll be on the same Dedicated Game Server (DGS) on the same shard.

Port Olisar is good for an example but not in practise which is why it will be going away, it is split into 4 landing area struts. 250 players per strut = 1000. That's only about double the players in a shard / DGS right now and current DGS's hold the whole of the Stanton system as well as Port Olisar.

There are 3 principles someone needs to understand to grasp what the plan for Star Citizen is going to become.

1. State change database and areas of authority.
Only one DGS can have authority over a defined area of the game space on a shard, but that defined area could be as small as a single room, or it could be as big as the whole game itself. Players on one shard cannot see or feel the effects of players or events on other shards (some information is exchanged between shards but it is limited).

If you have a base state for entity's (anything from a solar system, to a planet, to a cup) in the game then you only need to keep one copy of that entity in it's pristine state, this is why it is called the Replication Layer, because it replicates (copying), the pristine centrally stored copy of the world down to individual DGS's. When a server is spun up the data from the base state repository (Replication Layer Gateway Service) is written to the hard drive of the server, this is the way it was without PES. Every server had an identical copy of the Stanton system when it launched, fed only by player items - which are kept on a separate database. Once this process has completed the players can now enter that server shard.

Now with PES and Entity Graph you have the server loaded with the base state items for only a small part of the game world then you query the persistence database which only holds the details of any changes made to those base state items in that small area - and apply those changes example: location, orientation, damage state etc. Now before any player lands on a server it looks unique because change state information for that specific shard has been applied.

Change state for all entity's on a shard are constantly being written to, and read from the Entity Graph database. This is why there can't be more than one DGS with the same area of authority in the game shard, because conflicting information about the game zones condition would be written to the Entity Graph. You won't see 'invisible happenings' because to be in an area visible to you and other players you HAVE TO BE on the same DGS on a shard.

Again, to make it clear. There can only be one DGS that has authority over a given area in the game shard at any one time. There will not be two Port Olisar's on a shard. The way they populate a shard is by making each DGS's area of authority (in the game space) gradually less and less large. Let's say a DGS is holding a planet and it's moons, players are coming into that planetary system and that DGS is getting full - so while some players coming in are in QT travel 4 more DGS's are spun up on a new shard and the moons and planets now each go on their own separate server, as the shard with the overcrowded moon and planet is de-populated it is spun down.

There you go! you're getting it. There could be thousands of Dedicated Game Servers per shard and there could be dozens of DGS's for just one landing zone on a shard.

I've seen people talk about instances (copies) of locations within a shard. This is not particularly efficient, there's no need to instance within a shard if you can have as many shards as you wish and a single location Dedicated Game Server in a shard is no more 'expensive' system-wise per player than a multiple DGS Shard. We have single DGS shards now. There's no point in having 2 Lorvilles on one shard when I can have 2 Lorvilles on 2 shards for the same cost.

The main part of 'meshing' from the players perspective is the change from having to menu log into a location on a Dedicated Game Server to being able to seamlessly transition between DGS's. If it takes a few seconds to transfer a small group of players between DGS's where in the game are players limited to twiddling their thumbs for multiple seconds in a volume limited enclosed space? There's some other fancy services that run in the background designed to make intelligent and best use of those player transitions.

Your example about Lorville. Let's say 1000 players do decide to go there, can 1000 players fit in the same space all within sight of each other - not really. You can't get 1000 players into one elevator, there's only one way out of the hangar. Lorville is broken into areas, have you noticed all the twisty corridors where you can't see around the next corner? The sheer number of elevators! Think of all the separate areas in Lorville you can't get to without a train or an elevator, they can all be on their own Dedicated Game Server on a shard, it's not like one DGS for Lorville it could be up to 30 or 40 DGS's (each holding up to say.. 500 players) on the same shard with no area duplication. The train ride between all the gates and TEASA Spaceport? They are there partly to allow server meshing transitions to be less visible. Commuter Citizen was never about time sinks, it was about planning ahead to server meshing.

Let's say you land at Lorville, there's a crowd of 100 players milling about the area in the lobby of the Spaceport, the rest are spread out around Lorville, hab area, social / shopping area, hospital, 6 gates, business district.. (and more to come) and each of those locations are on their own DGS - you enter a new DGS via a train or an elevator and you leave that area to go to a new DGS area via a train or an elevator.

Those 100 players in the spaceport are making the system look for ways to offload some of the weight for new players to come into the spaceport, so as those players get on a train, 50 on one train 50 on another, they can't see inside a train they aren't on, so one train stays in the current shard and the other train is sent to another newly spun up shard. You can do this multiple times in the same time frame (I'm trying avoid using the word instant to avoid confusion), all the trains running around Lorville split and now you have reduced the population size of the shard, by shifting 50% of the population to a new shard while they were on a train in a black tunnel. As far as DGS transitions and shard transitions is concerned, trains (particularly in tunnels) and elevators are the same thing an opportunity to transfer players around as required either between DGS controlled spaces within the game or even between shards. That's why there are so damn many elevators and no stairs.

The system knows who your friends are, it knows if there was someone you were supposed to see and so it puts you on the shard where they are, and it moves all your 'stuff' to the shard you are on. All the other bodies who were at the Spaceport with you, if they have no reason to be on your shard you won't even notice they aren't with you anymore... you just think.. Oh, the other train occupants must have gone to other stations even if you were stood at the window you wouldn't know that train behind yours blinked out of existence in a black tunnel, it's not so crowded at the business district as it was at TEASA Spaceport. So if you are thinking about how can they split areas out to different DGS servers, or how can they hide transitions to other shards - think: train or elevator. Anywhere where the numbers of players are limited by space and they have to spend some time in them is where those transitions will occur.

Has anyone noted that the majority of security stop and searches go on around POI access points? When NPC activity is increased this is likely to be more so. There are those who want risk eliminated, but this is probably because they have an inflated view of risk and don't take into account risk reduction strategies.

How you navigate to those unavoidable POI's requires some 'out of the box' thinking. I think it was Sun Tsu who said that if you have 100 miles to go to a battle make sure the journey is made by the enemy, if you can achieve your goal by making that 100 mile journey into a 1000 mile journey with affordable cost to you, so much the better. There might be more efficient use of cooperating forces that reduces risk both to the defenders, which is a factor they will take into account, and to those who feel that standard techniques leave them open to being vulnerable. Anyone who doesn't do a cost benefit analysis of their choices is going to struggle to make any headway for long. Patience has it's own reward.

The OP in another thread has revealed that he is open to using the design of the system (beacons) to his advantage, it shouldn't come as a surprise that others can do the same with other aspects of the system. In the mind of the attackers they inherently think that confrontation is unavoidable and consequences are negligible they see every target as a juicy pay-off and themselves as virtually invincible. They see themselves as in place in every scenario without necessarily thinking how that occurs or what it would cost to achieve that, also traps (or subterfuge) that can be used for one can also be used for the other. Not all potential 'victims' will be dumb schmucks.

In the scenario of attacking a fully loaded Hull E going about it's lawful business there comes a point where there is a role reversal the attackers become loaders and haulers (otherwise what's the point?) and they don't have the protection of the system. The Hull E had ship insurance and cargo insurance, he's lost time. The ones hauling contraband have to get through all the checkpoints to a place where they can sell an uninsurable cargo, a place that will be known to bounty hunters, local security and even Advocacy. There is no reason to think that the security will be as pitiful as it is now. A certain percentage of that cargo will not get through and so the cost benefit analysis has to be made, is it worth it in the final analysis?

The current Stanton system is a goldfish bowl, it isn't yet as big as it's going to be and careful placement of future access points to trade can make big changes.

One of my favourite aspects of what is to come is that the game will be designed / is being designed (on balance) to reward the smartest, not the necessarily the strongest.

...and people say they don't listen to the community.

Just because you can't think of one, or other games you play don't allow for one, doesn't mean it doesn't exist.

EVE Online is only superficially like Star Citizen there is no first person physicality in EVE it has no facility react other than by choosing from menus once you are in a 'situation' you are locked into it, this isn't the case with Star Citizen. There is no DCS style combat play in EVE and there certainly is no first person gun play aboard ships, continuing the tired old argument that it is the same won't get anyone anywhere.

What has that got to do with it? The work was done by Cloud Imperium employees for that specific purpose, whether they finished it or not. It has a function and it has to be in place for the Replication Layer Gateway Service to work with Server Meshing.

I didn't miss it, I stated it explicitly - Entity Zones are nested within Object Containers. That still does not equate to... "...the fact 10 people in proximity to each other as when they are fighting require exponentially higher amounts of servers"... which is just nonsense. Am I surprised you selectively read what I wrote? No, not in the slightest.

The only part that might confuse some is that Chris uses the term Entity Zones in his Letter in place of Object Containers, once you realise that it's clear nothing has changed from the original plan. The hierarchical structure is still governed by the amount of players in a game region. Server Object Container streaming is still in effect.

The current build requires that all data for the Stanton system has to be written to the server, which has a max storage capacity and those data transfers to the server hard drive cost network bandwidth, with server meshing backed by Entity Graph those data writes are reduced to only those zones the players are currently using, thus saving cost.The Atlas Component Service (It's on the Progress Tracker) manages these data writes to Dedicated Game Servers.

The idea that ten players within fighting range of each other being on separated servers is just preposterous, what possible reason would there be to write the data for the same game zone to many servers if you don't have to? Why would they allocate network engineers for 62 weeks to make a service that is specifically designed to avoid that? Static Server Meshing breaks the game space into separated zones which have fixed boundaries of authority, the reason PES and Entity Graph was required before meshed servers is so that any unused zones can be spun down and then spun up in the exact same state they were last used so that only the zones the players are using needed to be loaded onto Dedicated Game Servers. The whole point of seamlessly meshed servers is to make more efficient use of servers with respect to player activity, stage one statically meshed servers is more efficient than standalone (which is what we have now) but not as efficient as dynamically meshed servers.

If your proposition is that they would go from one working system where a server can hold 100+ players to an exponentially less efficient system where servers can hold less than 10, after years of work and cost to change it, then you clearly have no idea what is planned. Any reasonable person would think to themselves, that can't be right, I must have misunderstood it... unless of course your agenda is permanently skewed by 'CIG bad'.

The assumption this woefully uninformed low effort at FUD OP is making is that no work has been done on the Replication Layer services as yet. A quick check of the Progress Tracker - Deliverables shows that work has been done on it.

Atlas - 62 weeks work completed - Add functionality to the Hybrid for what will become the Atlas component service of the Replication Layer. Atlas functionality splits the game up into multiple manageble (sic) regions (known as territories) which are then provided to the Replicant functions Dedicated Game Servers (DGS) by the Replicant Hybrid to manage and simulate.

Hybrid Service - 41 weeks work completed - Moves the network code's Replication Layer out of the Dedicated Game Server (DGS) and into a stand-alone service. This service is referred to as the Hybrid, as later versions of Server Meshing will split it into component services handling different aspects of the Replication Layer's functionality. The first version of Server Meshing will use the Hybrid service to manage client and server streaming, replication of networked state between clients and servers, and persisting state changes to the EntityGraph.

Replicated Entity Spawn Params From Network - 6 weeks work completed - Entity spawn parameters are a data record describing how to spawn a given entity. Previously these would be obtained from game code on the server and sent via the network to spawn entities on clients. This work pushes the necessary data into the network code'sReplication Layer so it can create entity spawn parameters independently of other systems.

Replication Layer Entity Authority - 73 weeks work completed - Moves the code that handles assigning and enforcing entity authority into the Replication Layer.

Server Streaming - 11 weeks work completed - Changes the implementation of Server Object Container Streaming (S-OCS) to be driven from the network code's Replication Layer, backed by EntityGraph for persistent storage.

Shard Replication Layer Population - 6 weeks work completed - Each Shard contains a complete independent copy of the game universe and its entity hierarchy. EntityGraph is the database providing persistent cloud storage for entities in the Shards and inventories. This work populates the Replication Layer for a Shard's server from the EntityGraph and allows changes to the persistent state to be written back.

StarHash Bind Culling - 5 weeks work completed - Bind Culling decides what entities are "bound" (network replicated) to which clients. Previously, the server would use the Entity Component Update Scheduler (ECUS) to determine visibility of entities for each client. This work introduces a StarHash maintained by the network code's Replication Layer to perform the same role. The StarHash is a data structure optimized for spatial queries, such as "what can this client see?"

There will be regional shards for quite a long time to come but that is more about real world signal travel time and bandwidth limits than any limits of CI's system... real world technological advances may answer that before CI needs to.

There's some very interesting work going on with fibre optics that may, probably, increase bandwidth (and reduce the number of required repeater stations on submerged cabling) by several orders of magnitude. It involves using different wavelengths of light to carry signals, each wavelength can carry the same amount of data that traditional white light adapters can. Those multiple inputs are joined using prisms to make white light which goes down the cable, at the other end the light is split again into it's constituent wavelengths to read each signal individually, apparently they are trialling a device to do this which is the size of a matchbox, they are scalable in series, so a matchbox that has 10 wavelengths can be put in series with 9 other matchboxes to make 100 times the bandwidth, and so on. Previously interference made this infeasible, but now there may be a way to overcome that (way above my pay grade to explain!). Ground stations equipped with multi-wavelength fibre optics linked to satellites may also reduce signal travel time considerably.

Let's take an analogy, just for a very rough example.

You are the person in charge of a National Park nature reserve. You have a group of staff and a budget. Someone comes up with a fantastic idea that all visitors to the park come with WiFi equipped cameras and they are constantly taking pictures, a lot of bird watchers!

So you ask an IT engineer, if we get the visitors to upload their pictures to our database can we use them to make a hyper-accurate population count of the number and types of birds we have in our park?

IT guy: We can set up the image database and network to collect the images then train an AI to recognise landscape features in the images and locate the position the photographer was in at the time the picture was taken to with 1 metre, all dated to the second.

Park Ranger: Great! How much will that cost and how long do you think it take?

IT Guy: Oh.. it will take about 10 engineers a year plus the cost of network and hardware - about 500 million dollars.

Park Ranger: Great! that's in our budget! Get started!

IT Guy: There is a problem.

Park Ranger: Oh, what's the problem?

IT Guy: There are two parts to what you are asking, you also want a system that will identify 'what is a bird' so that they can be counted.

Park Ranger: So how long would that take and how much?

IT Guy: We have to build a server farm, get a group of highly trained expensive AI research graduate guys to train an AI to go through all the images and recognise 'what is a bird' under any lighting conditions from any angle (birds are very good at camouflage!), or recruit and train about 500 ornithologists to go through every image manually and do a bird count - About 10 billion dollars and 5 years for the AI training. You have an average 10 million visitors per year taking about 20 images per visitor for the database so perhaps half that, 5 Billion dollars, to recruit and train 500 ornithologists, who will take about 15 years to go through one years worth of images. What is the average lifespan and breeding cycle of the birds in your park?

It seems simple to us to recognise a bird in a picture, the question is how do you train an AI to do it as efficiently or preferably several orders of magnitude much better to track bird populations in real time so that the information is current and useable, and cost effective?

Putting in a system to sell ships, especially since it's effects would be wiped periodically, might seem simple but it would be open to widespread abuse and so it would skew any analytical data they are collecting toward devising the final economic system, making it unusable. The argument that it would disrupt their fund raising is not valid, we already have non-monetary ways to obtain ships, you can just rent them - which you could see as temporary ownership. There are better ways to use their time and resources until ship selling becomes a valid proposition. The game is still being built, piece by piece. We are playtesting an alpha.

The 'simple' part is very often the hardest part. But don't worry, Cloud Imperium have a plan and you will get your wish... eventually.

Yes exactly, well explained. It's suits Entity Graph because of the Object Container heirachical structure. Only change states need to be stored and retrieved from a fixed starting point of a collection of object containers.

This probably / possibly explains why they switched from pad spawning to hangar spawning of ship object containers. With a pad open to view players would potentially see a ship spawned at base state and only then Graph database change state information applied.

This is why they switched from a serialised look up iCache database to Entity Graph which sorts it's database by dependencies. It is a better fit for SC than serialised look up's because SC uses object containers.

Graph based databases are a known technology that was developed to make faster customer database look up's much faster. The generational advance is Entity Graph, taking an application from one field and adapting it for their particular use. It's the kind of out of the box problem solving that Cloud Imperium encourage in their development team and that this community's support enables.
