The fisherman never gets all the fish in a river, not even close. He'll be happy to bag a couple per day or so. From the fish's point of view the numbers will always be on their side. But these fish have great memories and they can bite back when least expected.

If someone is being successful at bothering NPC's in the main because there is far more of them, there is no way to tell the difference between players and NPC's until you get within range of combat, but also a couple of players pissed off send the bounty up eventually to the point that this guy is attracting interest. He is being studied. The bounty amount makes it worth it for 3 amigo's to take the time to do the prep, they may not be the only team interested in this guy, only the winners get a payout. They know his preferred weapons, they know the places he goes to re-arm and repair. He has no idea who they are. They come into the system where he is and set up, they make their spawn point minutes away from where they know he is likely to be, they stock the local inventory with enough supplies so that they can each die and respawn up to 5 times. Easy done.

Well prepared they just have to catch him un-aware and even if he kills them a few times they can keep him pinned down until he either goes down or runs out of ammunition. If they go down they just respawn, if he goes down he goes to jail. Presuming the size of the bounty matches the crimes he could be there for a while. While he is in jail the 3 amigos set up for another 10 bounties in the same system, each time they send a guy to jail he's out of the system and the threat level to lawful players goes down. While they are active in the system the word goes out to lie low, don't expose yourself to anyone who knows they have a bounty out on them.

There is no limit to the total bounty the Advocacy can place on someone, there is no limit to the number of bounty-hunters who can share a contract. Multiple teams can choose to go after the same guy at once and they aren't even aware the others are after him. Local businesses feeling any disruption will be calling in the Advocacy and local security who will also be making bad guys lives difficult, further gradually reducing overall threat levels - most of the fish will just swim on by. The bad guys will withdraw further and further into areas they feel safer preferring their targets to come to them where they have the numbers.

Eventually an equilibrium will form, groups will have their own turf which they will defend against other bad guys coming in and upsetting the finely balanced apple cart as well as dealing with the good guys. A certain amount of chicanery will be tolerated especially if it is non-violent. A crazy-ass mass murderer jumping into the mix will just piss everyone off. This game has a memory that feeds back to the system in a way others don't. It's a cost benefit analysis, if the cost is too high to deal with lawlessness, they'll tolerate it. If the cost of not dealing with it is too high they will deal with it. The UEE gets taxes from traders, insurance companies don't like paying out. The UEE gets necessary supplies and interruption to those supplies will not be tolerated for long.

The lawless player will learn where to make their flea bites, and stay under the radar, or they will just give up on the idea and become bounty-hunters. For every black hat turned white hat the number of bad guys versus good guys goes down by a factor of 2. Most won't be able to sustain an interest in being lawless for long, they'll just get tired of the prison time or the restrictions it puts on their movement around the verse.

The Roadmap has the deliverable 'DGS Crash Recovery'. This means that if a server crashes you will stay in your game client while another server identical to the one that crashed is spun up and you will be seamlessly transferred to it where you can just carry on. This is the earliest form of the Server Meshing. All the player will notice is that for around a minute the game seems to stop responding, then it will carry on as if nothing happened.

If your 30K is due to a network disconnect it depends upon how long you were disconnected and they haven't said yet what they will do in that case.

The aim of Star Citizen is to give players choices, choices you don't get in the other games. You can choose to stay in safe areas, or go the risky route. You can even choose to stay put and never go anywhere, you don't have to fly a ship or shoot a gun. The amount of choice will be endless. The aim is to make local knowledge the key to any decisions the player makes, if you don't take the time to study your environment you potentially will suffer the consequences, this is the sort of depth most other games don't have.

There is a universe wide communications network that is always keeping people up to date with what is happening where.

You can have your own home base in SC.

You can move about the verse with hired / public transport, not likely to suffer much in the way of griefing since any disruption to in-game business trade will be met with security force intervention. Even if those transports are attacked it doesn't entail losing a whole lot to the passenger does it?

..and what about those levels of security force intervention? You have private, local and UEE with security checkpoints where-ever you go, as well as random checkpoints.

Are there prisons in Sea of Thieves?

Those who claim they can lord it over the lawful players always talk about combat in ships and in groups, but there will be times when they aren't in their ships, when they aren't going around mob-handed. They only have to be caught once to spend days perhaps weeks in prison. Every time they use a terminal their location is pinged and the bounty-hunters would be just as happy to come for them on foot.

What those who compare to other games completely forget is that the Living Breathing Universe will be full off things players will want to do and see, like luxury holidays and a Murray Cup Racing calendar, IAE and Invictus Week, and more - there won't be any quick wipe with a hack key, you could spend weeks in a prison. Your crime history stays with you for as long as your character lives. If you choose a lawless life it's for good and it will make a difference to where you can go and what you can do in the game universe.

When most of these who think they will be pirates give up on the idea, because they'll realise they can get their pew pew jollies just as much by being a bounty-hunter, which doesn't bring all the restrictions lawlessness does, then it's most likely going to be the dogs eating the dogs.

Every time someone tries to compare SC to other games they completely forget how big this game is not just in play space, but in the sheer amount of time and money sinks in the game. 10% of time taken away from from griefing means 10% more players have a happy time. Make a lawless player have to run from bounty-hunters 50% of the time and you have a player base that is over 50% happy. They will have to source their supplies from places in less safe areas and they'll cost more, they will take more effort to find.

These are calculations the small game brained don't take into account. They keep making the mistake of comparing other games to what SC is now, not what it will become.

A lot of these threads are just deliberate fear-mongering from ignorance.

I know they don't now, but they will in the future.

f lawless players are pinging they are giving up their location... and intent. As the OP says, an alert crew doing their job means the attacker has the harder job. Small animals survive in the wild even though they don't have the fastest legs, the biggest claws or the biggest teeth.

The fear of 'what ifs' stems from being uninformed about what is planned.

While I understand anyone's frustration at the length of time the project is taking, don't we all it was my 61st birthday yesterday, there is a point to note about that tracker - it doesn't include any work done that we are not told about. Of course the pessimistic assumption is always that there isn't any but I do not believe that is so. It also fails to take into account those features that have core tech dependencies, when those core techs go in we will find out more about what can be finally revealed. Too much is hidden behind Squadron 42 'spoilers' so that it is near impossible to make an accurate estimate of progress, however you feel about that, it is a fact.

The claim is often made that Chris deliberately gave false estimates, but there is video of him explaining why he chose to expand the scope of the project he had no idea that the community would be so wildly successful in providing for more funding and support than he ever expected back in 2012, it had more to do with the happenstance of opportunity aligning with the backer communities wishes than any pre-conceived notions he had at the start of the project. Judge that as you will, it is still a fact that he acknowledges he is building the community's game... not merely his first stated intent at his dream game.

Just because it hard to understand doesn't mean it is not true. If were simply a case of content additions or expansions then you could reasonably take the view that this live service is in some form of released state, but it isn't, there are core tech pillars still to go in and people need to understand that. Understanding that also brings into focus the scale of what is being made. While it may seem those of us who understand this are dogmatic in reinforcing this notion it needs to be remembered that every single time someone interacts with this game project those advisories regarding the state of development are in place, those who just click past them are no less dogmatic in insisting it isn't the reality.

The argument regarding the time it is taking is irrelevant because duration of a project is relative, you want cheap quick and easy? Yes you can expect that quickly, but this project has never been about cheap quick and easy.

It has always been my contention that they have worked on many more systems than we are aware of.

Yes but how often? The premise often forwarded by PVP-centric players is that it will be always a continual unavoidable occurrence, I don't agree with that, it discounts any forward planning players can use to lessen risk. Those wishing to engage in frequent gun action are going to hang out in high traffic areas, they aren't going to spend many hours out in the boonies on the off-chance of catching someone especially if the AI high traffic waterways are filled with bigger juicier fish.

Also while the increased AI traffic may bring more attackers, it also brings more bounty hunters, Advocacy, or even the navy - these are the unavoidable time-sinks the lawless players will face, directing their resources and time away from players. The game designers will balance this to avoid the gankfest often assumed by some.

I don't agree with that premise. It depends upon choices the player makes as to whether that will happen or not. It is Chris' stated intent that the most valuable resource to a players strategic planning will be local knowledge of any area they intend to enter. Even the AI will make a judgement whether it is worth their time and expense to operate in high security areas, and whether to allocate more security forces to quell illegal activity.

High security versus low security activity.

Depends on what your aim is, if it is to rush out a traditional game for release, then no it wouldn't be necessary. But that was never the aim of the project.

This is another one of those 'Barista' questions.

The issue isn't that you may not understand (traditional) game development but rather what the difference is between the way NPC's in Squadron 42 / Star Citizen undertake their tasks.

As you imply, in traditional games an NPC is scripted to perform a function in a specific area. That NPC will follow it's script identically each time, there will be a breakout animation (for example if the NPC is bumped or talked to, or engaged in combat) and then it goes back to following the script. 94 weeks would be a ridiculous amount of time if that was all this entailed.

This isn't the way NPC's are programmed in SQ42 / SC. They are environment aware, their tasks are part of their 'whole day' existence which they react to dynamically, they won't do the same thing time and time again. The mop and bucket guy in Squadron 42 for example is an interesting character, we've been told in the vertical slice mission, he isn't just a janitor - to put it in other game terms - he isn't just a Heimskr.

The process for making this character is the same they use for making other character behaviours... the 'mop and bucket' reference is their internal shorthand for this programming of active NPC's that will respond to any change in their environment and live a 24 hour existence.

There are many others who can give more detail than I can but IIRC the block size on Gen4 drives have caused issues, there is a registry fix for it.

What type of drive are you running the game on?
